    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_762609574" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/762609574" />
    <a title="cait" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25536510-cait"><img alt="cait" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582762314p2/25536510.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/762609574?book_show_action=true">Nov 11, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="cait" class="user" itemprop="url" name="cait" href="/user/show/25536510-cait">cait</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780152045609" href="/book/show/1045745.Heir_Apparent">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of scifi, people who like roleplaying games</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25536510-cait?shelf=library">library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25536510-cait?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer762609574" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17766104516865174337">I really don’t think you guys understand how much I mean it when I say: <b>This is seriously one of my favorite books of all time.</b><br/><br/>I read it for the first time when I was in middle school and I’ve read it several times since. Even now, at the geriatric old age of 24, I still absolutely adore this story. It’s everything I want, ties in so beautifully with some of my most excitingly dramatic fantasies, and <b>I JUST WANT IT TO BE MADE INTO A MOVIE SOSOSOSOSO BAD!</b><br/><br/><i>Heir Apparent</i> follows 14-year-old Giannine</span>
  <span id="freeText17766104516865174337" style="display:none">I really don’t think you guys understand how much I mean it when I say: <b>This is seriously one of my favorite books of all time.</b><br /><br />I read it for the first time when I was in middle school and I’ve read it several times since. Even now, at the geriatric old age of 24, I still absolutely adore this story. It’s everything I want, ties in so beautifully with some of my most excitingly dramatic fantasies, and <b>I JUST WANT IT TO BE MADE INTO A MOVIE SOSOSOSOSO BAD!</b><br /><br /><i>Heir Apparent</i> follows 14-year-old Giannine Bellisario as she ventures to an arcade for her birthday. The novel is set in a futuristic society not far outside the realms of our own reality in which public busses speak and can be spoken to (but aren’t very intelligent) and arcades house immersive virtual reality games. Giannine settles on a game entitled Heir Apparent and is promptly cast into the role of shepherd’s daughter who discovers, after the death of the king, that her parents are only her foster parents, she is the secret bastard child of the king and his former mistress, and she must return to the palace to claim her rightful place as heir to the throne. Forced to face off against three half siblings and the queen, peasant unrest, barbarian attacks, and a very choose-your-own-adventure style gaming experience, Giannine knows she’s in for a challenging game. Until a group of activists breaks into the arcade and trashes the equipment, making it impossible for staff to safely remove her from the game before completion and leaving her in a fight for her life: <b>Beat the game soon if you want to survive.</b><br /><br />Every time I pick up this book, I’m terrified that I’m not going to love it as much as I have in the past. That maybe I glamourized it in my head or was in the right frame of mind when I read it, but that it’s not that good. Every time, it proves me wrong.<br /><br />I genuinely love this story and the characters. It’s so visually appealing to me in a way that many books are not, managing to paint these vivid images in my head and bringing to mind the most exquisite sets I can imagine. It appeals to me, also, as a part-time gamer, former R.L. Stine <i>Choose Your Own Adventure</i> book reader, and forever daydreamer.<br /><br />The setting is unique in that it’s repetitive. Every time Janine (as she’s called in the game) dies, she awakens in a sheep field, covered in feces, with her foster mother calling her name. She’s forced to experience the same series of events over and over, make decisions on how to interact with those around her and who to ally herself with, and find herself killed in sinister, bizarre, and treacherous ways. She is motivated by one thing and one thing only: To stay alive in the game so that she can stay alive in the real world.<br /><br />I love watching her actions effect the world around her. Every round, she makes slightly different decisions and, while some things are always the same – her interactions with her foster family, her introduction to the royal family (when she makes it to the Great Hall), the boy being dragged to the courtyard for poaching – things vary every time she makes a decision – the results of the barbarian attacks, the support/betrayal of the guards, Kenric’s behavior towards her.<br /><br />And I still find it absolutely fascinating.<br /><br />I’d be lying if I pretended that I don’t have a bit of a crush on Princes Wulfgar and Kenric. (Mostly Kenric.) When Janine allies herself with either of them, it’s always going to be a fun time, filled with sly smiles and strangely enjoyable interactions. I’d also be lying if I denied that I really want the Barbarian King married off to both the Queen and Sister Mary Ursula, just for the laughs and to get them out of our hair.<br /><br />I honestly don’t know what to say about this book beyond the fact that I am absolutely in love with it. I wish that the princes weren’t her brothers so there could have been a romance, but that sounds kind of creepy right now, so maybe I should stop.<br /><br />All I know is that the ending is perfection, I love Kenric’s response to her tears as her brain finally begins to overheat right before she manages to beat the game (even if he was programmed to react that way), and meeting Nigel Rasmussen and hearing his perspective on Kenric as a character makes me so happy every single time. <br /><br />The only thing I’d change? I’d like it if Kenric had looked at her the moment they all hailed Janine as King and said “You win” before everything collapsed around her. I feel like that moment of awareness/conclusion in the midst of what was happening would have just pushed it even a little bit farther for me.<br /><br />You win. The end.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17766104516865174337" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1304876" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1304876" />
    <a title="Emma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/75857-emma"><img alt="Emma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1556514715p2/75857.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1304876?book_show_action=true">May 18, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma" href="/user/show/75857-emma">Emma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of fantasy and/or the movie &quot;Groundhog Day&quot;</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1304876" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4941743248239230053">Vivan Vande Velde is one of the best fantasy writers out there. Her stories are believable and populated with characters you'll remember long after the book is closed. Her stories are also surprisingly believable given that they are fantasies. Such is the case with this novel, which takes place in some undisclosed future time. The story gets into gear when the narrator, Giannine, enters a full-immersion virtual reality game (by the same name as the title of the book) to compete to rule a kingdom</span>
  <span id="freeText4941743248239230053" style="display:none">Vivan Vande Velde is one of the best fantasy writers out there. Her stories are believable and populated with characters you'll remember long after the book is closed. Her stories are also surprisingly believable given that they are fantasies. Such is the case with this novel, which takes place in some undisclosed future time. The story gets into gear when the narrator, Giannine, enters a full-immersion virtual reality game (by the same name as the title of the book) to compete to rule a kingdom. The problem? If Giannine loses she might not be able to leave the game environment.<br /><br />As you might have guessed by that little summary, most of this story revolves around Giannine playing the game over and over as she tries to win. This creates a lot of repetition--as we watch Giannine go through the same scenarios repeatedly with varying levels of success (If this sounds similar to the premise of "Groundhog Day" that's because it is.). Happily, instead of seeming redundant, the story/plot remains interesting. Vande Velde artfully describes the gameplay so that readers won't get bored. This makes the book go by really fast.<br /><br />The characters are extremely interesting and the premise--while not totally new--is unique, as is the author's handling of it. The story features Vande Velde's usual humor throughout. What it doesn't feature is her usual ambiguous ending. The story is still open-ended but it has more closure than are found in A Well-Timed Enchantment or Companions of the Night (both also by Vande Velde and also highly recommended), which makes for a nice change.<br /><br />You can find this review and more on my blog <a href="http://www.missprint.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Miss Print</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="4941743248239230053" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_18568594" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eshusdaughter" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eshusdaughter" href="/user/show/742623-eshusdaughter">Eshusdaughter</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/742623-eshusdaughter?shelf=read-in-2008">read-in-2008</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/742623-eshusdaughter?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/742623-eshusdaughter?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/742623-eshusdaughter?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer18568594" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1415615696479528001">I'll be honest, I mostly picked up this audiobook because it was narrated by Carine Montreband and I was so in love with the Uglies books by Westerfeld that she narrated that I wanted to hear her voice again. The unconscious mental comparison between Westerfeld's book and this one may be skewing my opinion of it. <br/><br/>Summary: Fourteen-year-old Giannine becomes trapped in the virtual reality game Heir Apparent when an activist group attacks the gaming center where she's playing. Suddenly the safety m</span>
  <span id="freeText1415615696479528001" style="display:none">I'll be honest, I mostly picked up this audiobook because it was narrated by Carine Montreband and I was so in love with the Uglies books by Westerfeld that she narrated that I wanted to hear her voice again. The unconscious mental comparison between Westerfeld's book and this one may be skewing my opinion of it. <br /><br />Summary: Fourteen-year-old Giannine becomes trapped in the virtual reality game Heir Apparent when an activist group attacks the gaming center where she's playing. Suddenly the safety measures that are supposed to protect her aren't there and every time Giannine dies in the game she edges closer toward a fatal brain overload.<br /><br />Overall, the story stretched out too long for me and seemed rather thin. It was frustrating how many times Giannine had to start over and the same events repeated. While Giannine faced some tough decisions and lots of machinations, the pacing was just off. There needed to be more action and more happening. Too often it felt like Giannine was just floating along in the game, buffeted by various forces. The fact that none of the characters she was interacting with were real, and the reader knew that, also made it hard to form any sort of attachment to them. The characters were just a program with no personal consciousness and thus no real stake in the outcome of the story.<br /><br />The dialogue and description are well done throughout and this is a well-written story. It's missing a spark however to take it from so-so to a really good book. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1415615696479528001" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer21681766" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4301595984327108420">One of my favorite books because it combines fantasy and reality, as well as future-tech gaming with present-day frustrations. But besides the content, I continue to be amazed by the way the book is set up. The main character Giannine is stuck in a virtual fantasy game in which death can occur to the protagonist. Every time Giannine 'dies,' she begins anew from the the start, able to revise her decisions and react differently to the opportunities and threats presented to her. As she goes through</span>
  <span id="freeText4301595984327108420" style="display:none">One of my favorite books because it combines fantasy and reality, as well as future-tech gaming with present-day frustrations. But besides the content, I continue to be amazed by the way the book is set up. The main character Giannine is stuck in a virtual fantasy game in which death can occur to the protagonist. Every time Giannine 'dies,' she begins anew from the the start, able to revise her decisions and react differently to the opportunities and threats presented to her. As she goes through the game differently, the other characters react to her differently as well. I admire this unusual way of telling a story, as well as the effort needed to create characters who are recognizable despite their new reactions.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4301595984327108420" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1035021225" />
    <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl"><img alt="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603085284p2/8734459.jpg" /></a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=ya-fantasy">ya-fantasy</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=not-my-cuppa-tea">not-my-cuppa-tea</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=library-has">library-has</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1035021225" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4713309226527524529">This book has the unique accomplishment of being on both my YA science fiction and YA fantasy shelves. It's a fantasy RPG (role playing game) with magic, dragons, princesses, etc., wrapped in a SF shell (technology gone wrong). <br/><br/>The main character is a 14 y/o girl, Giannine aka Janine, who is playing a total immersion RPG that requires her to prove herself the rightful heir to the throne and overcome conniving relatives, dragons, rebelling peasants, an angry king of a neighboring country (his mag</span>
  <span id="freeText4713309226527524529" style="display:none">This book has the unique accomplishment of being on both my YA science fiction and YA fantasy shelves. It's a fantasy RPG (role playing game) with magic, dragons, princesses, etc., wrapped in a SF shell (technology gone wrong). <br><br>The main character is a 14 y/o girl, Giannine aka Janine, who is playing a total immersion RPG that requires her to prove herself the rightful heir to the throne and overcome conniving relatives, dragons, rebelling peasants, an angry king of a neighboring country (his magical crown was stolen by Janine's father) and various other problems typical of a fantasy RPG. Unfortunately, almost as soon as she starts the game, it malfunctions because of some misguided protesters. Giannine/Janine needs to win the game so it will end before the technology fries her brain in real life. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379799432i/654686.jpg" width="284" height="241" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>If you've ever been into role-playing fantasy games, you'll probably enjoy this. It's a cute story and kind of fun, if you like this kind of thing. But I always got bored when I used to watch my brothers playing these games, trying to break through to the next level, starting over at the beginning every time you die, needing to replay the same scene over and over . . .<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1417820958i/12554108.jpg" width="330" height="330" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> </span>
  <a data-text-id="4713309226527524529" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1048064375" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1048064375" />
    <a title="ambyr" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2670408-ambyr"><img alt="ambyr" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451339945p2/2670408.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1048064375?book_show_action=true">Sep 07, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="ambyr" class="user" itemprop="url" name="ambyr" href="/user/show/2670408-ambyr">ambyr</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780152045609" href="/book/show/1045745.Heir_Apparent">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2670408-ambyr?shelf=author%E3%85%A1female">authorㅡfemale</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2670408-ambyr?shelf=romantic-subplot-i-did-not-want">romantic-subplot-i-did-not-want</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2670408-ambyr?shelf=genre%E3%85%A1science-fiction">genreㅡscience-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2670408-ambyr?shelf=protagonist%E3%85%A1female">protagonistㅡfemale</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2670408-ambyr?shelf=acquired%E3%85%A1from-work">acquiredㅡfrom-work</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2670408-ambyr?shelf=age%E3%85%A1ya">ageㅡya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2670408-ambyr?shelf=i-am-not-the-right-audience">i-am-not-the-right-audience</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1048064375" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6733585668691285772">This book is an excellent example of how much the YA genre has shifted over the past decade. I read a fair amount of current YA, and while I'm technically old for it, I'm clearly not that far out of the marketing department's sights. <i>Publishers Weekly</i> informs me that today's YA is generally aimed at the sixteen to twenty-five set.<br/><br/>But <i>Heir Apparent</i> was published in 2002, when YA was still aimed firmly at young adults--that is, at kids who hadn't yet left home. Even if I'd found in 2002, when I wa</span>
  <span id="freeText6733585668691285772" style="display:none">This book is an excellent example of how much the YA genre has shifted over the past decade. I read a fair amount of current YA, and while I'm technically old for it, I'm clearly not that far out of the marketing department's sights. <i>Publishers Weekly</i> informs me that today's YA is generally aimed at the sixteen to twenty-five set.<br /><br />But <i>Heir Apparent</i> was published in 2002, when YA was still aimed firmly at young adults--that is, at kids who hadn't yet left home. Even if I'd found in 2002, when I was still a teenager albeit one a couple years into her college career, I'm pretty sure I would have found it painfully young. The protagonist is fifteen, but if anything I'd say this book is targeted at twelve- or thirteen-year-olds, following the classic "make the protagonist older than the audience" formula of middle-grade fiction.<br /><br />I will say this for Giannine: unlike the protagonists of many of today's YA novels, she's convincingly teenaged. Unfortunately, at this point I'm far enough removed from teenagerhood that this only makes me sigh and grit my teeth. And yet I kept reading, because the game Giannine plays was genuinely compelling to me. I'm fascinated by game design, and I thought Velde's description of Heir Apparent the game managed to walk the line of telling a compelling story that still seemed believably programmable as a computer game. I was glad we got to see so many forks and wish I could explore others.<br /><br />Sadly, that plot kept getting interrupted by the frame plot, which mostly just annoyed the hell out of me. It made the unfortunately frequent error of raising the states <i>too</i> high, by which I mean I knew the author was never going to make good on the threat so it provided none of the tension it should have. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Specifically, the frame story has Giannine trapped within her game by a terrorist attack that fried the computer, preventing her from being disconnected safely by third parties; if she doesn't win, she'll die. But this is a first-person novel aimed at middle school students. I had exactly zero fear that the protagonist would actually die, and I'm pretty sure I would have felt the same if I'd read it when I was twelve. It doesn't take that much genre savvy to work it out.<br /><br />It's unfortunate, because I can think of so many better frame stories. Giannine has parent issues out the wazoo; maybe one of her parents could have been an excellent gamer whose reputation she was trying to live up to, or maybe there could have been a cash prize for the game that would have given her the money she needed to finally initiate a visit to one of her parents on her own terms. In either case, there would still have been an external motivation for Giannine to win . . . but there also would have been real tension about whether Giannine would succeed in gaining parental approval/time, or whether she would need to learn how to do without. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />And then there's the broader frame story, which is painfully unsubtle. "This book is dedicated with affection for, but no patience with, those who would protect our children through humorless moralizing and paranoia about fantasy," says the dedication, and <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[of course, in the story, it's anti-fantasy protestors who put Giannine's life at risk by damaging the game terminal she's playing on. Of course it is. I honestly find myself wondering if the author realized that her adventure novel made playing fantasy games sound dangerous and swapped ecoterrorists for save-our-children-terrorists at the last second just to make sure the moral aligned with her own beliefs. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Minus one star for blunt-force moralizing, and we get a solid two stars. Recommended only for the pre-high school set.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6733585668691285772" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9347057794857150252">Heir Apparent is one of my favourite middle grade books. Rereading it more than 10 years later, it's every bit as good as I remember. It doesn't have the most original premise-- getting stuck in a high stakes virtual reality game --but Giannine's narrative voice makes it special. I love her dry, sarcastic take and all the puzzle-solving. <br/><br/>Pairs well with <b>Hexwood</b> by Dianna Wynne Jones.</span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer111241841" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17339592570060345218">This is another book I find myself rereading at least once every year. That could just be because I am a video game fan, and this book is about a virtual reality video game, or just because it’s a damn good read.<br/><br/>Of course, it’s also one of those books that pulls off the stunt of “changing something” that’s always worked a certain way, but the way it was pulled off… you didn’t even know it was happening until the very end when they mentioned it.<br/><br/>The writing style is easy to understand, and flows b</span>
  <span id="freeText17339592570060345218" style="display:none">This is another book I find myself rereading at least once every year. That could just be because I am a video game fan, and this book is about a virtual reality video game, or just because it’s a damn good read.<br /><br />Of course, it’s also one of those books that pulls off the stunt of “changing something” that’s always worked a certain way, but the way it was pulled off… you didn’t even know it was happening until the very end when they mentioned it.<br /><br />The writing style is easy to understand, and flows beautifully. The descriptions allow one to imagine the landscape and people around you, but also leaves room for your own imagination to think up its own version. And although it’s a short book that can be devoured in a scant few hours, those few hours will not be wasted.<br /><br />A truly sublime book, and I recommend it to any and all, not just the video game fans.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17339592570060345218" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3586618475" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17212108505776019148">Light fantasy or early LitRPG, this is much better than the first book in the series. Decent female lead character, but the story is a little rushed at times. A very quick read.<br/><br/>For the majority of the book there is only one person; the rest are computer driven characters. Playing a one hour session (a birthday present) she is trapped in the game when anti-gamer terrorists attack the game center, breaking the immersion device somehow. She can only exit the game by winning, and if she fails to do </span>
  <span id="freeText17212108505776019148" style="display:none">Light fantasy or early LitRPG, this is much better than the first book in the series. Decent female lead character, but the story is a little rushed at times. A very quick read.<br /><br />For the majority of the book there is only one person; the rest are computer driven characters. Playing a one hour session (a birthday present) she is trapped in the game when anti-gamer terrorists attack the game center, breaking the immersion device somehow. She can only exit the game by winning, and if she fails to do that soon, she will probably die in real-life.<br /><br />Okay, hokey setup, but it works. When she dies in-game, she restarts from the very beginning, though that doesn't happen too often. She must live by her wits. This is good for her and enjoyable to read. The computer characters have an excuse to be 2D, but they do have differing individual motivations. Working out the permutations is another part of the challenge.<br /><br />So yeah, I liked it. The strongest reviews seem to be mostly people fondly remembering this from their youth. The first book in this universe was in 1990 (and only average), this book 2002. Another was written in 2012 - perhaps we are due for a fourth. I plan to read the third book regardless.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17212108505776019148" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_57544746" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/57544746" />
    <a title="Trish" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1544645-trish"><img alt="Trish" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1224227679p2/1544645.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/57544746?book_show_action=true">May 27, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trish" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trish" href="/user/show/1544645-trish">Trish</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer57544746" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2546630508900217199">What I liked about this book was the idea that you could build an entire story just to make a statement. I suppose that's all anyone ever does when they write, but it was obviously done. Before you even begin the story, there is the page that is made to look like a gift certificate, which sets the tone for what's in store. It's a ticket for the reader to come along to another world within another world--just as the main character goes, too. And then at the end, in case you were taken in by a pri</span>
  <span id="freeText2546630508900217199" style="display:none">What I liked about this book was the idea that you could build an entire story just to make a statement. I suppose that's all anyone ever does when they write, but it was obviously done. Before you even begin the story, there is the page that is made to look like a gift certificate, which sets the tone for what's in store. It's a ticket for the reader to come along to another world within another world--just as the main character goes, too. And then at the end, in case you were taken in by a prince's smile, you are reminded that the bigger purpose of the story is the political statement with a final page made to look like a picketing sign. There is also an invitation to start your own protest. It made me smile and I thought, "Well done, Vivian Vande Velde."<br /><br />I like that the author tries to empower a young crowd to take a stand and think for themselves. While I have no objection to the reading of scriptures, it is my belief that shouting thee's and thou's from a picket line is in strong opposition to the way religious texts were intended to be read. For this same reason, I don't speak that way in normal everyday language. I would rather honor my religious beliefs in a quiet manner. If anyone would ask me directly, with real intent on answers, I would not be afraid to share the deepest feelings of my heart, but I do not agree with broadcasting it in political spheres.<br /><br />For those that would censor books or games, I believe their motives and intentions come from a good place. There is a big difference in movie ratings from the 80's versus today or rather there is more awareness thanks to concerned parents who spoke up. My parents took me to R-rated movies growing up, and I became desensitized to the embarrassment of watching people suck face on screen. I have not allowed my children to be in the same situation and would rather preserve their childhood for as long as possible. I don't want them to be desensitized to something that they naturally turn their faces away from. And they do! Even when watching TV shows or commercials today. They prefer not to look.<br /><br />Aside from political statements, the story was a good one. I like the kind of video games where you have to talk to others to find out what your objective is, so I appreciated the game being played in the book. The story unfolds much the same way one level of Super Paper Mario unfolds, only without jumping on goombas. Unlike, Super Paper Mario, there isn't just one path, but an infinite number of paths to take based on individual choices. Also, it was like Tron, being inside the game itself. All in all, I think I would enjoy playing Heir Apparent.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2546630508900217199" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_567045549" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/567045549" />
    <a title="Harold Ogle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/198484-harold-ogle"><img alt="Harold Ogle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1317340769p2/198484.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/567045549?book_show_action=true">Mar 21, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Harold Ogle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Harold Ogle" href="/user/show/198484-harold-ogle">Harold Ogle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/198484-harold-ogle?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/198484-harold-ogle?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/198484-harold-ogle?shelf=cyberpunk">cyberpunk</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/198484-harold-ogle?shelf=gaming">gaming</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/198484-harold-ogle?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/198484-harold-ogle?shelf=dragons">dragons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/198484-harold-ogle?shelf=shapechangers">shapechangers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/198484-harold-ogle?shelf=divorce">divorce</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer567045549" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17336615245609764963">A fun read, <u>Heir Apparent</u> is a story about a near-future girl stuck in a VR game (resulting from a terrorist attack) with only a little time to win the game before her nervous system collapses from prolonged exposure to the VR stimuli. Apparently it's second in a series, but I had no idea, as this was another random selection from the library. Also, the author makes it clear that this was written - at least in part - as a reaction to fundamentalists and others who rail against the value of fanta</span>
  <span id="freeText17336615245609764963" style="display:none">A fun read, <u>Heir Apparent</u> is a story about a near-future girl stuck in a VR game (resulting from a terrorist attack) with only a little time to win the game before her nervous system collapses from prolonged exposure to the VR stimuli. Apparently it's second in a series, but I had no idea, as this was another random selection from the library. Also, the author makes it clear that this was written - at least in part - as a reaction to fundamentalists and others who rail against the value of fantasy and gaming, claiming that it is harmful to children.<br /><br />It's a fun conceit, because it gives the sense of playing an adventure game (particularly the old Sierra games, in which you can and do die on every screen): she repeatedly makes sensible choices and finds that someone kills her. In the game, this results in her having to start over, but in real life, she's used up even more of what little time she has left before her brain fries permanently. So this adds a bit of a mystery element to the reading of the book: as the reader, you are also trying to divine what the correct choices would be to succeed.<br /><br />In the game, called 'Heir Apparent,' our protagonist Giannine (for once just a child of divorced parents, rather than an orphan) becomes the bastard Princess Janine, who has been raised in secrecy by shepherds (a minor irritation here: Velde repeatedly refers to Janine as a 'shepherder,' rather than the more traditional 'shepherdess' or the correct 'shepherd.' It's weird.) until the King names her his heir on his deathbed. This naturally doesn't sit well with his queen, or any of his three legitimate sons, the Princes who expected one of them would inherit the crown. Winning the game requires that she survive to the succession ceremony, and the game is a challenge because there are so many people who want her dead. In addition to her murderously envious half-siblings, there is a peasant uprising, an invading barbarian horde, an infestation of ghosts, and a rampaging dragon to handle. I really enjoyed the book and found the game plot very interesting.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17336615245609764963" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_219969387" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/219969387" />
    <a title="Faith " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6575284-faith"><img alt="Faith " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1317950156p2/6575284.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/219969387?book_show_action=true">Oct 06, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Faith " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Faith " href="/user/show/6575284-faith">Faith </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer219969387" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3562822651297940434"> It was Giannine Bellisario’s fourteenth birthday, when she received a gift certificate to a gaming center, given to her from her ignorant, and un involved Father. To get into this gaming center, she had to get through the Citizens to Protect Our Children (CPOC) first. Once she was in Rasmussem Gaming Center, the games began. The place was filled with virtual games, and she had to decide which to choose. Giannine selected the virtual game, Heir Apparent, but she was limited on time. The time in </span>
  <span id="freeText3562822651297940434" style="display:none"> It was Giannine Bellisario’s fourteenth birthday, when she received a gift certificate to a gaming center, given to her from her ignorant, and un involved Father. To get into this gaming center, she had to get through the Citizens to Protect Our Children (CPOC) first. Once she was in Rasmussem Gaming Center, the games began. The place was filled with virtual games, and she had to decide which to choose. Giannine selected the virtual game, Heir Apparent, but she was limited on time. The time in the virtual game was longer than what the actual time was. She needed to do everything possible to keep her from dying, and to get to her goal. Every time Giannine dies in the game it starts over, but there is a problem, she is trapped in the game with limited time. Before everything goes bad, she needs to finish what she stared and the only way to do this is to finish the game.<br /><br /> I was a little mixed on my rating of this book, I feel that the author did a great technical job of writing this book, but I don’t know personally if I enjoyed the idea of it. It seemed as if I was reading the book three times over, for the text of this book was repetitive and not quite enough engaging. I believe that the audience of this book is more towards, Sci-Fi fanatics, and more so teenage boys. This book had a few young adult ready phrases, which younger audiences might not understand. All in all this book was very well written, but maybe not so much of my type of book and not so much for others of the ages of 11 and younger. For I think that this book appeals to the audiences of futuristic behaviors. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3562822651297940434" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Bearing in mind that this is a children's book, the aim is targeted to making good decisions. So I ignored the obvious plot hole at the beginning. Honestly, it was frustrating to listen to the repetitive nature of the first 20%. But on reflection, the protagonist is 14 years old and t</span>
  <span id="freeText9498625136833366018" style="display:none">I picked up this book for a r/fantasy reddit reading prompt as LitPRG written by a woman. <br /><br />In the game Heir Apparent, the player is a sheep-farmer's daughter who is suddenly thrust into ruling in a medieval kingdom. Bearing in mind that this is a children's book, the aim is targeted to making good decisions. So I ignored the obvious plot hole at the beginning. Honestly, it was frustrating to listen to the repetitive nature of the first 20%. But on reflection, the protagonist is 14 years old and therefore will make quite a few mistakes and making the voice suitable for the age. After this initial bump, things did improve and the story was enjoyable. The author uses this story to reflect on dysfunctional family and its cost, beauty for teenage girls and was never preachy. <br /><br />Overall, I rated this as 3.5 stars. I would listen to another book in this series, and I am defintely willing to read another book in this genre. Even though I am not a gamer. </span>

<div id="review_876298004" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/876298004" />
    <a title="Jenna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2404793-jenna"><img alt="Jenna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1492534675p2/2404793.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/876298004?book_show_action=true">Mar 08, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenna" href="/user/show/2404793-jenna">Jenna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer876298004" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6390021483792806253">I was super into the premise of this book, especially the (I thought) overarching theme of censorship, specifically the feverish censorship of children and the media (or anything, really) available for consumption. The opening scenes of the main character having to enter the gaming center through rabid, protesting parents was so powerful, alluding, I am sure, to the experience of women entering an abortion clinic in our political climate. Off to a good start, I thought! Powerful and believable. </span>
  <span id="freeText6390021483792806253" style="display:none">I was super into the premise of this book, especially the (I thought) overarching theme of censorship, specifically the feverish censorship of children and the media (or anything, really) available for consumption. The opening scenes of the main character having to enter the gaming center through rabid, protesting parents was so powerful, alluding, I am sure, to the experience of women entering an abortion clinic in our political climate. Off to a good start, I thought! Powerful and believable. I know by reading some reviews on here, tha the pacing of the book dissuaded some people to review it higher but, in a story where something is bound to happen over and over, you have to know that it might get a little redundant. I actually think the author did very well on that account. Not too slow and, just when it was repeating too much, the next time the character re-spawned, the beginning events were even more briefly described. The book itself is written a little young for my taste but I wouldn't count it against this story as I am a 26yr old reading about a protagonist who is 14; I can't be too surprised about that. There were, however, a couple of issues that just rubbed me the wrong way. <br />Again, I was interested in the premise of this book and doubly so as it stars a girl gamer (yay, lady gamers!) but my illusions of a more thoughtfully crafted protagonist were shattered as soon as she asked the receptionist if the castle RPG she was looking to play was for girls too. Maybe that's a product of the gaming companies in our universe promoting games mainly to a male audience but, as a female FPS player, I don't hem and haw over the new Call of Duty title and wonder if I can play it too! I know a lot of feminists and maybe it's just their hardcore views of the affronts they read into every little thing (not that I don't agree most of the time) but there were just times in the book where I'm like, stop being terrible, girl! There was some offhanded comments made about a heavier-set women in the game (from whom the game forced our main character to borrow clothes when the other characters all hated her) and some unsavory (to me) comments about the ridiculously beautiful sorceress who is so gorgeous that she apparently wouldn't just elicit envy from other women but would also cause them to seek plastic surgery. I mean, what? I was a teenage girl once, I know how terrible you can feel or be made to feel about your body, but it's really not necessary to allude to that in a fantasy game setting. It kind of reinforces that kind of thinking which is really sad. Just when I thought I was being over dramatic, I found this quote: <br /><br />"She sighed. Loudly. 'Physical appearance is not what is important.'<br />Yeah right. Tell that to any girl who hasn't bothered to put on a presentable shirt or fix her hair because she's only running into the grocery store to get a quart of milk for her grandmother, and who does she see tending the 7-ITEMS-OR-LESS cash register but the guy of her dreams, except she can't even say hi—much less try to develop a meaningful relationship—since she looks like the poster child for the terminally geeky".<br /><br />Like I said, it's a legitimate thought a young girl might have but it just sort of makes body shaming/self shaming cyclical. Maybe if I was younger I would see it for what (I hope) the true intention was: "This girl is just like me! She likes video games and has the same thoughts and emotions that I do!". But I really don't think it added anything to this book.<br /><br />Also, the fact that she awakens at the end of the book in the hands of a young, worried, disheveled, handsome, genius, multi-billionaire made me roll my eyes real hard and make a lot of dumb fart noises with my mouth. <br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="6390021483792806253" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1923570593" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13575212116423284709">I loved this book, read it in 6th grade I believe. I've been trying to locate it so I can re-read it, and it has taken me literal years to find it again. I'm still considering re-reading, to refresh my memory and all. My favorite line, I'll always remember, was along the lines of "your mother was a toaster oven" (Velde, Heir Apparent)</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_64470278" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/64470278" />
    <a title="Arminzerella" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1769011-arminzerella"><img alt="Arminzerella" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1275503782p2/1769011.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/64470278?book_show_action=true">Jul 21, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Arminzerella" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Arminzerella" href="/user/show/1769011-arminzerella">Arminzerella</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1769011-arminzerella?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1769011-arminzerella?shelf=young-adult-fiction">young-adult-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1769011-arminzerella?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1769011-arminzerella?shelf=borrowed-from-the-library">borrowed-from-the-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1769011-arminzerella?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1769011-arminzerella?shelf=gutsy-girls">gutsy-girls</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1769011-arminzerella?shelf=suspense-thriller">suspense-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1769011-arminzerella?shelf=role-playing-games">role-playing-games</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer64470278&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer64470278" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16373264468762914019">Giannine gets a gift certificate for her birthday to a Rasmussem Gaming Center, a virtual reality environment where your brain is hooked up to Rasmussem equipment so you can have the ultimate immersive gaming experience. Giannine decides to play Heir Apparent, a game in which the main character finds herself the unexpected heir to a throne, but faces all sorts of opposition from other NPCs (non-player characters). She’s just settling into her game when she gets a strange message from Nigel Rasmu</span>
  <span id="freeText16373264468762914019" style="display:none">Giannine gets a gift certificate for her birthday to a Rasmussem Gaming Center, a virtual reality environment where your brain is hooked up to Rasmussem equipment so you can have the ultimate immersive gaming experience. Giannine decides to play Heir Apparent, a game in which the main character finds herself the unexpected heir to a throne, but faces all sorts of opposition from other NPCs (non-player characters). She’s just settling into her game when she gets a strange message from Nigel Rasmussem himself – the gaming center where she’s currently playing was attacked by a group of People from the Society to Protect Our Children and they’re unable to unhook her from the gaming equipment without possibly damaging her brain. Also, she’s only got half an hour (3 days in game time) to win the game before things get critical for her. The only way Giannine can make it out of the game is to win. And, like any other video game, she’s got to muddle through by trial and error. Nigel gives her some hints, but they’re not enough to tell her what she needs to do. So Giannine has to figure out her own way of doing things.<br /><br />This had a satisfying beginning, which got a bit muddled and frustrating after Giannine started losing…over and over and over again. She’s resilient, though, because she has to be (there’s no other way). She can’t get frustrated like you might with a video game because her life depends on her success. The choices she makes are interesting, and the narrative really does capture the experience of this sort of gaming. D&amp;D or role-playing enthusiasts would probably enjoy this (or rip it up depending on their expertise), and fantasy lovers might get into it as well. A gaming friend of mine wanted to know more about the technology behind the virtual reality experience, and why it was timed – he wasn’t willing to suspend his disbelief for that. <br /><br />This was not what I’d expected – I thought it was going to be straight up fantasy, but it had a science fiction basis, mixed with a fantasy setting. A very cool idea, and not too badly executed. I’d like to read others like this, with a bit more sophistication.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16373264468762914019" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_169948176" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/169948176" />
    <a title="Emily" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622519-emily"><img alt="Emily" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573581765p2/4622519.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/169948176?book_show_action=true">May 21, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily" href="/user/show/4622519-emily">Emily</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622519-emily?shelf=sci-fi-fantasy">sci-fi-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622519-emily?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer169948176" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17679879968586932975">As a avid gaming fan myself, I was overcome with giddiness when I learned that the main protagonist of this fun read about a gamer trapped inside a medieval virtual reality strategy setup was also a female. I give major one-ups to V-cubed (Vivian Vande Velde) for not making this seem like a big deal. Rather, she just stated that girls can also like games, so let's get on with the awesome adventures, shall we? <br/><br/>Giannine is witty, smart and believably determined as your typical 14-year-old girl une</span>
  <span id="freeText17679879968586932975" style="display:none">As a avid gaming fan myself, I was overcome with giddiness when I learned that the main protagonist of this fun read about a gamer trapped inside a medieval virtual reality strategy setup was also a female. I give major one-ups to V-cubed (Vivian Vande Velde) for not making this seem like a big deal. Rather, she just stated that girls can also like games, so let's get on with the awesome adventures, shall we? <br /><br />Giannine is witty, smart and believably determined as your typical 14-year-old girl unexpectedly caught in something out of her league (however, not too determined to be distracted from from the handsome boys in the game). As someone who has played various versions of Zelda for hours on end (Ocarina of Time, anyone?), the strategic set up of this game made me wish it was real. An experienced gamer will wag a finger at the novice mistakes Giannine makes in the beginning (hint: extraneous characters are usually not extraneous), but she soon catches onto the trends of the gameplay as the adventures become more complicated and the stakes become even greater. The highest of all stakes, of course, is that Gianinne's non-virtual life also hangs in the balance, with the time ticking away until the machine overloads ...unless she can beat the game. This scenario is wonderfully fun to follow, even if I've seen it in other books and television shows before (most memorably in a kickass episode of Are You Afraid of the Dark?). <br /><br />Aside from the main plot, HA has great thematic undercurrents about how the true dangers are often not the video games or virtual realities, but those who would try to censor kids from experiencing these worlds. As a fantasy novelist, this campaign felt both relevant and genuine coming from VVV. This was perfectly addressed in the beginning of the novel, and then smartly tossed aside in order to let the adventure take over. <br /><br />All in all, this is a fast-paced adventurous ride that has a lot to love about it. I think I would have definitely enjoyed it more if I was a few years younger (I am admittedly out of range of the target audience), but even so I would recommend this to anyone looking for a fun way to spend the afternoon. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17679879968586932975" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_219947162" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/219947162" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/219947162?book_show_action=true">Oct 06, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amber" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amber" href="/user/show/6561060-amber">Amber</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer219947162" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9831378843282812221"> The book Heir Apparent, by Vivian Vande Velde, is about a girl named Giannine Bellisario who gets sucked into the video game Heir Apparent. Giannine is turning fourteen and her father gives her a gift certificate to the gaming arcade called the Rassmusem Gaming Center. To start off the beginning of a “fantastic” day she has to pass the CPOC (Citizens to Protect our Children). Once she gets in, she has a few games to pick from. She chooses a game where they completely put you and make you feel l</span>
  <span id="freeText9831378843282812221" style="display:none"> The book Heir Apparent, by Vivian Vande Velde, is about a girl named Giannine Bellisario who gets sucked into the video game Heir Apparent. Giannine is turning fourteen and her father gives her a gift certificate to the gaming arcade called the Rassmusem Gaming Center. To start off the beginning of a “fantastic” day she has to pass the CPOC (Citizens to Protect our Children). Once she gets in, she has a few games to pick from. She chooses a game where they completely put you and make you feel like you are participating in the game. Then the CPOC damaged the equipment to the game and she is stuck in the game. The only way to get out of there unharmed is to win the game. In a regular video game when you die you get another life and start off where you died. In Heir Apparent you have to start all the way from the beginning and go through the whole game again. This is a huge problem because there are a lot of complications in the game that can make you die. Will she ever become the king and win the game?<br /> Heir Apparent was a well written book. It was suspenseful in some parts and others it was just like you were reading through something that had no interesting parts in it. In some parts of the book I felt like the author had mentioned the same parts of the story and started to get tired of it. The author could have used more descriptive/ vivid words and more understandable phrases. Some parts of the book were very confusing and I didn’t understand what was happening. Other parts I didn’t even pay attention to what I was reading because there were phrases that I didn’t want to read. I would recommend this book to readers that are really interested in future/medieval types of books. It wouldn’t be a book for kids in 5th grade or below. Even though this book wasn’t one of my favorites it did have parts/chapters that I enjoyed. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9831378843282812221" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2948374022?book_show_action=true">Sep 05, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Olivia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Olivia" href="/user/show/61277553-olivia">Olivia</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2948374022" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5437571774111918446">This book was a ton of fun. It was pure escapism, and I absolutely flew through it. I loved the “choose your own adventure” game atmosphere. The story itself was rather bare bones (get to the end of the game, or you die [in the real world!]). That being said, sometimes I prefer simple narratives and this one really worked. This story was also absolutely hilarious. The narrator’s choices, internal monologue, and reactions to her circumstances were laugh out loud funny. My main critique of this st</span>
  <span id="freeText5437571774111918446" style="display:none">This book was a ton of fun. It was pure escapism, and I absolutely flew through it. I loved the “choose your own adventure” game atmosphere. The story itself was rather bare bones (get to the end of the game, or you die [in the real world!]). That being said, sometimes I prefer simple narratives and this one really worked. This story was also absolutely hilarious. The narrator’s choices, internal monologue, and reactions to her circumstances were laugh out loud funny. My main critique of this story is that the heroine was supposed to be a teenager but really came across as an adult. Her reactions to certain situations and the way in which she navigated challenges read as more mature than a 14 year old. That being said, if you’re interested in this story and want to pick up a fun, quick science fiction read, I’d recommend this one. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5437571774111918446" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9411489-reading-is-my-escape?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9411489-reading-is-my-escape?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1599301176" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3941200760261653528">Virtual Reality Fantasy Game <br/>I was going to die. I was never going to get past the first step of the game, and I was going to die. <br/>-Chapter 4<br/> <br/>Between the barbarian hordes waiting at our northern border for the first sign of weakness, and the peasant uprisings in the east, now is not the time for an inexperienced sheepherder to play at being king.<br/>-Chapter 8<br/> <br/><br/>Giannine is playing a virtual reality game called Heir Apparent, using a gift certificate from her father for her 14th birthday. But, a prote</span>
  <span id="freeText3941200760261653528" style="display:none">Virtual Reality Fantasy Game <br />I was going to die. I was never going to get past the first step of the game, and I was going to die. <br />-Chapter 4<br /> <br />Between the barbarian hordes waiting at our northern border for the first sign of weakness, and the peasant uprisings in the east, now is not the time for an inexperienced sheepherder to play at being king.<br />-Chapter 8<br /> <br /><br />Giannine is playing a virtual reality game called Heir Apparent, using a gift certificate from her father for her 14th birthday. But, a protest group attacked the facility and now Giannine is stuck in the game. Her only way out is to win the game, but her time is limited. If she doesn't defeat the game, the computer could fry her brain. She must use her intelligence and her sarcastic sense of humor to keep going, figure out the puzzles and be crowned king before time runs out.<br /> <br />I enjoyed this book. It is a fresh take on sci-fi. Giannine lives in the future, but she plays a virtual reality game that takes her to medieval times. Most of the time we are with Giannine in the game and it is exciting and frustrating to watch her try to get through the situations with no idea what the right choice is.<br /> <br />Giannine is a great strong female character. She is clever and persistent, but she still has flaws. She gets annoyed and frustrated by her lack of progress, but she never gives up. She has to deal with ghosts, a dragon, barbarians and a royal family who doesn't want her around.<br /> <br />Recommended to:<br />Grades 4-8. Readers who enjoy fantasy and adventure.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3941200760261653528" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1629475096" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1629475096" />
    <a title="Darla" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1365026-darla"><img alt="Darla" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1629475096?book_show_action=true">May 04, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Darla" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Darla" href="/user/show/1365026-darla">Darla</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1629475096" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13792454191082839480">(Genre:Children's fiction (or younger teen)/science fiction/fantasy) This was an interesting story about a young teenager who enters a virtual reality gaming center while protestors are picketing outside (they are concerned about the effect these virtual reality games have on the brains and development of society, and more especially, the youth). Once she is hooked up into the game, the protestors cause a disruption to the service, which leaves her trapped in the game until she can finish it. Un</span>
  <span id="freeText13792454191082839480" style="display:none">(Genre:Children's fiction (or younger teen)/science fiction/fantasy) This was an interesting story about a young teenager who enters a virtual reality gaming center while protestors are picketing outside (they are concerned about the effect these virtual reality games have on the brains and development of society, and more especially, the youth). Once she is hooked up into the game, the protestors cause a disruption to the service, which leaves her trapped in the game until she can finish it. Unfortunately, the game's creator is concerned that she will fry her brain if she is hooked up to the game for too long and they are unable to safely disconnect her as well. However they are able to enter the game briefly to let her know what is going on and to give her some hints as how best to proceed, as she tries to bring the game to a satisfactory conclusion.<br />I really enjoyed the premise of this story line as it felt realistic to our society today--protestors resorting to violence or destruction of property, which causes greater damage and harm, rather than truly promoting their cause. The main character's journey thru the computerized scenario was humorous--each time she was "killed" she would materialize back at the beginning of the story and have to analyze where her choices had led her wrong as she repeated her "game". It was fascinating how much her progress in the game was related to very small choices she made along the way. And of course there was the ever threatening time constraints to solve it. I quite liked it! 3.5 stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="13792454191082839480" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText1400598679776167998" style="display:none">Giannine Bellisario (Thea Greenleaf) is back in this fun filled fantasy adventure.<br /><br />Giannine is raised by her grandmother, and when her absent father asks her what she wants for a birthday present she of course asks for a Rasmuesen gift card. To bad CPOC has to ruin her perfectly harmless adventure...<br /><br />CPOC, an organization devoted totally to the "Protection of Our Children" attacks the Rassmuesen facility and damages the machines. With Giannine fully submerged in her adventure and the damaged equipment attached directly to her brain this presents a full fleged problem. <br /><br />Nigel Rassmuesen, CEO of the Rasmuesen company and inventor of the games is horrified to discover that the girl in the game may be the first fatality that the gaming industry has ever seen, scared he uses some of the energy left in the game to project himself into the game and warn Giannine, but he can do nothing else- her life rests in her own hands as she races against the clock to win <i>Heir Apparent</i>...<br /><br />Heir Apparent, the fantasy role playing game that became so much more to Giannine, not just a fun game, but a phisically dangerous adventure. Three Princes, one Princess, one Queen a barbarian King- who to trust? This question is the delicate balance between life and death in this fantasy-science fiction, were nothing is as it seems and the clock is merciless in its ticking, so hurry up Giannine, solve the puzzle before it is to late- or it is GAME OVER- <u>forever</u>!<br />Tick Tock...</span>

<div id="review_509927090" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Kirsten Simkiss" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16550352-kirsten-simkiss"><img alt="Kirsten Simkiss" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1540600215p2/16550352.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
